R: 2, Systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE), 30,  The presence of malar rash, arthritis, lymphadenopathy, and cutaneous ulceration could be consistent with SLE. However, the predominance of muscle weakness and dermatomyositis-specific skin findings make SLE less likely.
R: 3, Muscular dystrophy, 20,  Progressive proximal muscle weakness, easy fatigue, and falling episodes could be seen in muscular dystrophies. However, the presence of skin findings and systemic features make muscular dystrophy less likely.

R: 2, Systemic Lupus Erythematosus (SLE), 15,  The presence of malar rash, muscle pain, and lymphadenopathy could indicate SLE, another autoimmune disorder that can affect multiple organ systems.
R: 3, Polymyositis, 10,  The proximal muscle weakness and muscle pain or tenderness are consistent with polymyositis, an inflammatory muscle disease. However, the skin manifestations are less common in this condition.
R: 4, Muscular Dystrophy, 5,  Progressive proximal muscle weakness and easy fatigue could be signs of muscular dystrophy, a group of genetic disorders causing muscle weakness and wasting. However, the skin manifestations and lymphadenopathy are not typically associated with muscular dystrophy.
R: 5, Viral Myositis, 5,  Certain viral infections can cause muscle inflammation, leading to weakness, pain, and tenderness. The presence of lymphadenopathy supports this possibility, but the skin manifestations are less likely in viral myositis.
